    "conventionally , electric transport in bulk materials is characterized by the conductivity @xmath1 .",
    "then , the conductance @xmath2 of a finite - size sample of dimensions @xmath3 can be found by combining the conductances of its smaller parts , @xmath4 .",
    "this description , however , is applicable only at sufficiently high temperatures , at which the conductivity can be treated as a local quantity .",
    "it was discovered about two decades ago  @xcite that the quantum corrections to the conductivity are non - local on the scale of the ( temperature dependent ) dephasing length @xmath5 , which is much larger than the elastic mean free path .",
    "if the sample is small , or the temperature low , so that @xmath6 exceeds the sample size , the concept of conductivity loses its meaning .",
    "moreover , the conductance @xmath2 acquires significant sample - to - sample fluctuations and can no longer be treated as a self - averaging quantity . for a temperature @xmath7 below the thouless energy @xmath8 , these sample - to - sample fluctuations are of the order of the conductance quantum @xmath9 , independent of sample size or mean free path ( @xmath10 is the time it takes for an electron to diffuse through the system ) .",
    "this phenomenon is called `` universal conductance fluctuations '' ( ucf ) , and it was studied in great detail both theoretically and experimentally , see  @xcite for a review .",
    "it is important to emphasize that the lack of self - averaging of the conductance is a feature of _ mesoscopic _ samples , _",
    "i.e. _ , samples with linear dimensions smaller than @xmath5 but still much larger than the fermi wave length .",
    "these ideas that defined the field of mesoscopic physics were initially developed in the context of transport through disordered metals .",
    "a convenient way of creating more controllable mesoscopic samples was developed with the use of semiconductor heterostructures , see @xcite for a review .",
    "as the electron motion in these systems is quantized in the direction perpendicular to the plane of the heterostructure , a two - dimensional electron gas is formed at the interface between the layers . with the help of additional electrostatic confinement , usually in the form of metal gates deposited on top of the hetrostructure , the two - dimensional electron gas ( 2deg )",
    "can be tailored to form a finite - size sample , referred to as a quantum dot .",
    "its size , shape , and connection with the rest of the 2deg can be controlled by means of a sophisticated system of electrostatic gates , see fig .",
    "[ fig1 ] .",
    "= 0.8    links connecting the quantum dot to the 2deg ( quantum point contacts ) are characterized by the number @xmath11 of electron modes ( or channels ) propagating through the contact at the fermi level , and by the set of transmission probabilities for these modes . with the increase of the point contact cross - section",
    ", the number of modes , @xmath11 , is increasing .",
    "if the boundaries of the point contact are smooth on the length scale set by the electron wavelength , then the contact acts as an electron wave guide  @xcite : all the propagating modes , except the one which opened last , do not experience any appreciable backscattering . for the last mode ,",
    "the transmission coefficient varies from @xmath12 to @xmath13 in the crossover from the evanescent to propagating behavior  @xcite . in the specific case of a gate - controlled contact ,",
    "see fig .",
    "[ fig1 ] , the distance between the gate and the depleted edge of the 2deg is typically large compared to the electron wavelength in the electron gas  @xcite .",
    "the curvature radius of the edge of the 2deg at the contact is of the order of this distance , and therefore the smoothness condition is satisfied .",
    "a statistical ensemble of quantum dots can be obtained by slightly varying the shape of the quantum dot , the fermi energy , or the magnetic field , keeping the properties of its contacts to the outside world fixed .",
    "statistical properties of the conductance for such an ensemble depend on the number of modes , @xmath11 , in the junctions and their transparency .",
    "the `` usual '' ucf theory adequately describes the conductance through a disordered or chaotic dot in the limit of large number of modes , @xmath14 .",
    "when all channels in the two point contacts are transparent , the universal value of the root mean square ( r.m.s . )",
    "conductance fluctuations @xmath15 is much smaller than the average conductance @xmath16 .",
    "the distribution of conductances is essentially gaussian , and can be found theoretically by means of the standard diagrammatic expansion for disordered systems  @xcite , or with random matrix theory ( rmt ) , see refs .",
    "@xcite and @xcite for reviews . upon closing the point contacts ( _ i.e.",
    "_ , decreasing @xmath11 ) , the average conductance decreases whereas the r.m.s .",
    "fluctuations retains its universal value . at @xmath17 , the fluctuations and the average of the conductance are of the same order , and the conductance distribution function is no longer gaussian .",
    "still , if one neglects the interaction between the electrons , the statistics of the conductance can be readily obtained within rmt @xcite .",
    "the rmt of transport through quantum dots can be easily justified for non - interacting electrons",
    ". however , real electrons are charged , and thus interact with each other .",
    "it is known from the theory of bulk disordered systems , that the electron - electron interaction results in corrections to the conductance  @xcite of the order of unit conductance quantum @xmath9 . for a quantum dot connected to a 2deg by single - mode junctions ,",
    "this correction is not small anymore in comparison to the average conductance @xmath18 .",
    "we see that at @xmath19 and low temperatures , both mesoscopic fluctuations and interaction effects become strong .",
    "quantum interference and interaction effects can not be separated , and there is no obvious expansion parameter to use for building a theory describing the statistics of the conductance in this regime .",
    "this paper reviews the current understanding of physical phenomena in a wide class of mesoscopic systems  quantum dots  under the conditions in which effects of electron - electron interaction are strong .",
    "a first step to approach this problem is to disregard the mesoscopic fluctuations altogether .",
    "it means that one neglects the random spatial structure of the wave functions in the dot and the randomness of the energy spectrum ; the discrete energy spectrum with spacing @xmath20 between the one - electron levels in a closed dot is replaced by a continuous spectrum with the corresponding macroscopic density of states . for realistic systems , this approach can be justified sometimes at not - so - low temperatures .",
    "the remaining problem of accounting for the coulomb interaction is non - perturbative at small conductance @xmath21 , and therefore still not trivial .",
    "it constitutes the essence of the so - called coulomb blockade phenomenon  @xcite .",
    "the coulomb blockade manifests itself most profoundly ( see , e.g. , ref .",
    "@xcite ) in oscillations of the dot s conductance @xmath22 with the variation of the voltage @xmath23 on a gate , which is capacitively coupled to the dot , see fig .",
    "[ fig2 ] . the resulting dependence @xmath22 exhibits equidistant coulomb blockade peaks separated by deep minima ( coulomb blockade valleys ) .",
    "the peaks occur at the charge degeneracy points , _",
    "i.e. _ , specific values of @xmath23 at which changing the dot charge by a single quantum @xmath24 does not cost any energy .",
    "the idea of the coulomb blockade was suggested in the early experimental paper  @xcite in the late 1960 s , though the term `` coulomb blockade '' was coined only two decades later  @xcite . a quantitative theory in terms of rate equations describing the transport through a blockaded quantum dot or metal grain at @xmath25 ,",
    "was formulated in ref .",
    "@xcite , and was generalized to systems with a controllable gate in ref .",
    "this theory is commonly referred to as the `` orthodox theory '' .",
    "the main conclusion of the orthodox theory is that the conductance through a blockaded grain at low temperatures is exponentially suppressed .",
    "the first experiments on gated metallic coulomb blockade systems were reported in ref .",
    "@xcite .",
    "= 0.8    at larger values of the dot s conductance ( corresponding to larger values of the conductances @xmath26 and @xmath27 of the point contacts connecting the dot to the outside world ) , the orthodox theory and , eventually , the phenomenon of coulomb blockade break down because of quantum fluctuations of the charge in the dot . the fluctuations destroy the coulomb blockade at the value @xmath28 .",
    "quantum fluctuations affect both transport properties ( such as linear conductance and @xmath29-@xmath30 characteristics ) and thermodynamics ( _ e.g. _ , differential capacitance ) .",
    "the @xmath29-@xmath30 characteristic in the coulomb blockade valleys at relatively small conductance was considered in  @xcite in second order perturbation theory in @xmath2 ; later the corresponding non - linear contribution to the current found in  @xcite became known as `` inelastic co - tunneling ''  @xcite .",
    "corrections induced by charge fluctuations at @xmath31 were calculated in  @xcite for the thermodynamic characteristics , and in  @xcite for the linear conductance . at @xmath31 the problem of quantum charge fluctuations was mapped  @xcite on the multi - channel kondo problem  @xcite , which in some cases can be solved exactly  @xcite .",
    "another limit which allows for a comprehensive solution , is the case of a point contact with one almost open conducting channel linking the dot to the lead ( conductance @xmath2 is close to the conductance quantum )  @xcite . in this limit , and still neglecting mesoscopic fluctuations ( @xmath32 ) , the coulomb blockade almost vanishes : the contribution periodic in the gate voltage @xmath23 to the differential capacitance , which is the prime signature of coulomb blockade , is small compared to the average capacitance  @xcite .",
    "moreover , it was shown within this model that the coulomb blockade disappears completely in the case where the channel is fully transparent .    in all of the aforementioned works the effects of mesoscopic fluctuations , associated with the finite size and the discrete energy spectrum of the isolated dot ( nonzero level spacing @xmath20 ) ,",
    "were ignored .",
    "however , these fluctuations drastically affect the results . in open dots ,",
    "mesoscopic fluctuations reinstate periodic oscillations of the differential capacitance and conductance as a function of the gate voltage @xmath33 , as a remnant the charge discreteness in the dot , even in the limit of completely transparent channels in the point contacts .",
    "if the dot is almost closed , the chaotic nature of the wave functions in the dot gives rise to mesoscopic fluctuations of observable quantities .",
    "both in the coulomb blockade valleys and at the peaks , the conductance turns out to have large fluctuations , and is very sensitive to a magnetic field .",
    "our main goal in this paper is to review the rich variety of effects associated with the finite level spacing @xmath20 , the chaotic nature of the wave functions , and the coulomb interaction for both closed and open dots .",
    "here is a one - paragraph guide to the review .",
    "sections  [ sec:2 ] ,  [ sec:3 ] , and  [ sec:4 ] are devoted , respectively , to the physics of an isolated quantum dot , transport through a dot weakly connected to leads , and thermodynamic and transport properties of a dot connected to lead(s ) by one or two almost reflectionless quantum point contacts .",
    "we begin in section  [ sec:2 ] with the formulation of the model describing the statistical properties of the system .",
    "we clarify the conditions of the equivalence of the usual diagrammatic technique and random matrix representation , and establish the validity of the capacitive interaction approximation .",
    "the central result of this part can be found in subsection  [ sec : hfinal ] , where we present the universal form of the interaction hamiltonian describing the dot , and estimate the accuracy of the universal description . in section  [ sec:3 ]",
    "we review the theory of mesoscopic fluctuations of the conductance in peaks and valleys of the coulomb blockade , and the theory of the kondo effect in quantum dots .",
    "weak dot - lead coupling allows us to use the familiar technique of the perturbation theory in tunneling strength .",
    "we believe it makes section  [ sec:3 ] easy to read .",
    "nevertheless , a very pragmatic reader who wants to grasp the main results first , without going through the details , may start by reading the summary in subsection  [ sec : tdependence ] .",
    "section  [ sec:4 ] deals with the similar phenomena in quantum dots connected to leads by transparent or almost transparent point contacts , where the interplay between quantum charge fluctuations and mesoscopic physics becomes especially interesting .",
    "methods described and used in section  [ sec:4 ] are technically more involved than in section  [ sec:3 ] , and include the bosonization technique along with the effective action formalism . to make the navigation through the material easier",
    ", we decided to start this section with a presentation of the main results for the conductance through a dot and for its thermodynamics , see subsection  [ sec : overall ] .",
    "along with providing the general picture for the conductance and differential capacitance , this subsection points to formulas valid in various important limiting cases , which are derived later in subsections  [ sec : cap][sec : g ] .",
    "subsections  [ sec : finitesize][sec : open ] review the main physical ideas built into the theory , while the details of the rigorous theory are presented in subsection  [ sec : rigorous ] .",
    "last but not least , we illustrate the application of theoretical results by briefly reviewing the existing experimental material , see subsections  [ sec:3.1][sec : kondo ] , and  [ sec : dos ] .",
    "in subsections  [ sec:2.1 ] and [ sec : mf ] we discuss the electronic properties of an isolated quantum dot . under the assumption that electron motion inside the dot is chaotic , we establish a hierarchy of energy scales for the free - electron spectrum : fermi energy , thouless energy , and level spacing .",
    "the correlation between electronic eigenstates and eigenvalues can be described by random matrix theory ( rmt ) if the difference between the corresponding energy eigenvalues is smaller than the thouless energy . in subsection",
    "[ sec : interaction ] we proceed with the inclusion of effects of the interaction between the electrons .",
    "it is shown that the two - particle interaction matrix elements also have hierarchical structure .",
    "the largest matrix elements correspond to charging of the quantum dot , as described by the charging energy in the constant interaction model .",
    "finally , open quantum dots are discussed in subsection  [ sec:2.2 ] , where we introduce the hamiltonian of the junctions connecting the dot with the leads and relate the parameters of this hamiltonian to the characteristics of the quantum point contacts .",
    "let us start from a picture of non - interacting electrons , postponing the introduction of electron - electron interactions to sec.[sec : interaction ] .",

    "each particular eigenstate depends sensitively on the details of the random potential @xmath36 , which is determined by the shape of the quantum dot",
    ". however , we will not be interested in the precise value of observables that depend on the detailed realization of the potential @xmath36 .",
    "instead , our goal is a statistical description of the various response functions of the system with respect to external parameters such as magnetic field , gate voltage , etc . , and of the correlations between the response functions at different values of those parameters .",
    "hereto , the statistical properties of a response function are first related to the correlation function of the eigenstates of the hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.2 ] ) .",
    "then , we can employ the known results for statistics of the eigenvalues and eigenvectors in a disordered or a chaotic system  @xcite .    for a disordered dot ,",
    "the correlation functions are found by an average of the proper quantities over the realizations of the random potential .",
    "such averaging can be done by means of the standard diagrammatic technique for the electron green functions @xmath41 where plus and minus signs correspond to the retarded ( r ) and advanced ( a ) green functions respectively .",
    "the spectrum of one - electron energies is fully characterized by the density of states @xmath42 , \\label{eq:2.5}\\ ] ] where the last equality follows immediately from the definition ( [ eq:2.4 ] ) . even though the density of states is a strongly oscillating function of energy ,",
    "its average is smooth , @xmath43 where @xmath44 is the mean one - electron level spacing .",
    "it varies on the characteristic scale of the order of the fermi energy @xmath45 , measured , say , from the conduction band edge , which is the largest energy scale in the problem .",
    "since we are interested in quantities associated with a much smaller energy scale , we can neglect the energy dependence of the mean level spacing .",

    "@xcite , and one finds @xmath91      physical properties of a mesoscopic system are manifestly random . the statistics of the random behavior can be studied by a measurement of the fluctuations caused by the application of an external magnetic field @xmath92 .",
    "the role of such a field is primarily to alter the quantum interference pattern . as a result , the characteristic fields which significantly affect the properties of a mesoscopic system are rather weak in a classical sense :",
    "the cyclotron radius of an electron remains much larger than the linear size of the dot , and the effect of the magnetic fields on classical trajectories can be neglected .",

    "this conclusion allows for a simple semiclassical interpretation of the relation ( [ eq:2.101 ] ) between @xmath144 and the real magnetic field @xmath92 , as we now explain .    consider a classical trajectory of an electron starting from a point @xmath161 and returning to the same point , see fig .",
    "[ figabflux ] .",
    "the quantum mechanical amplitude for this process contains an oscillating term @xmath162 , where @xmath163 is the classical action along this trajectory . in a weak magnetic field",
    "the classical trajectory does not change , while the classical action acquires an aharonov - bohm phase : @xmath164 where @xmath165 is the directed area swept by the trajectory , see fig .",
    "[ figabflux ] .",
    "if the time it takes for the electron to return along the trajectory , @xmath166 , would be of the order of the ergodic time @xmath167 , the characteristic value of this area would be of the order of the geometrical area of the dot @xmath168 ( the meaning of the thouless energy @xmath159 is discussed in previous subsections ) .",
    "if , however , @xmath169 , the electron trajectory covers the dot @xmath170 times .",
    "each winding through the dot adds a value of the order of @xmath171 to @xmath165 ; these contributions , however , are of random signs , ( an example is shown in fig .  [ figabflux ] ) .",
    "therefore , the total area accumulated scales with @xmath172 , @xmath173 the orthogonal ensemble is different from the unitary ensemble by the fact that in the orthogonal ensemble the quantum mechanical amplitudes corresponding to a pair of time reversed trajectories have the same phase , while these phases are unrelated for the unitary ensemble . for a small magnetic field ,",
    "this means , that the trajectories which acquired an aharonov - bohm phase smaller than unity still effectively belong to the orthogonal ensemble whereas , those which acquire a larger phase are described by the unitary ensemble . to obtain the characteristic time scale separating these two regimes , we require @xmath174 substituting estimate ( [ eq:2.108 ] ) into eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.109 ] ) , and using @xmath175 , one finds @xmath176 up to a numerical coefficient , this estimate coincides with the energy scale given by eqs .",
    "( [ eq:2.106 ] ) and ( [ eq:2.101 ] ) .",
    "the small energy scale physics is governed by long trajectories with a typical accumulated flux larger than the flux quantum . for such trajectories the interference between the time reversal paths",
    "is already destroyed . at larger energy scales , the contributing trajectories are shorter , and they do not accumulate enough magnetic field flux to destroy the interference .",
    "= 0.6    [ figabflux ]      let us now turn to the discussion of interaction between electrons in a quantum dot . in the basis of eigenfunctions @xmath177 of the free - electron hamiltonian , the two - particle interaction takes the form : @xmath178 hereinafter , we will write explicitly the spin indices @xmath1 for the fermionic operators . the generic matrix element of interaction is : @xmath179    our goal is to show that the matrix elements of the interaction hamiltonian also have hierarchical structure : only a few of these elements are large and universal , whereas the majority of them are proportional to the inverse dimensionless conductance @xmath180 , and thus small  @xcite . as the result ,",
    "hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.14 ] ) will be separated into two pieces : @xmath181 the first term here is universal , does not depend on the geometry of the dot , and it does not fluctuate from sample to sample for samples differing only by realizations of disorder . the second term is small as a power of @xmath180 , and it fluctuates .",
    "this term only weakly affects the low - energy ( @xmath182 ) properties of the system .",
    "the form of the universal term can be established using the requirement of compatibility of this term with the random matrix model ( [ eq:2.11 ] ) .",
    "since the random matrix distribution is invariant with respect to an arbitrary rotation of the basis , the operator @xmath183 may include only operators invariant under such rotations . in the absence of the spin - orbit interaction , there are three such operators : @xmath184 the operator @xmath185 is the total number of particles , @xmath186 is the total spin of the dot , and operator @xmath187 corresponds to the interaction in the cooper channel .",
    "( for the unitary ensemble the operator @xmath187 is not allowed . )",
    "gauge invariance requires that only the product @xmath188 of the operators @xmath189 and @xmath190 can enter into the hamiltonian . at the same time , @xmath191 symmetry dictates that the hamiltonian may depend only on @xmath192 , and not on separate components of the spin vector .",
    "taking into account that the initial interaction hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.14 ] ) is proportional to @xmath193 , we find for its universal part : @xmath194 the three terms in the hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.152 ] ) have a different meaning .",
    "the first two terms represent the dependence of the energy of the system on the total number of electrons and total spin , respectively . because both total charge and spin commute with the free - electron hamiltonian",
    ", these two terms do not have any dynamics for a closed dot .",
    "we will see that the situation will change with the opening of contacts to the leads .",
    "finally , the third term corresponds to the interaction in the cooper channel , and it does not commute with the free - electron hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.1 ] ) or ( [ eq:2.11 ] ) .",
    "this term is renormalized if one considers contributions in higher order perturbation theory in the interaction . for an attractive interaction , @xmath195 , the renormalization enhances this interaction , eventually leading to the superconducting instability .",
    "( we will not consider the case of an attractive interaction here ; for a recent review on the physics of small superconducting grains , see ref .",
    "effects in larger grains , @xmath196 , are reviewed in ref .",
    "@xcite . ) for the repulsive case , @xmath197 , this term renormalizes logarithmically to zero .",
    "we will be dealing with the latter case throughout the paper .",
    "constants in the hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.152 ] ) are model - dependent . in the remainder of this subsection",
    "we will show how to calculate them for some particular interactions and discuss the structure of the non - universal part @xmath198 .",
    "at this point it is important to mention that universal hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.152 ] ) is defined within the hilbert space of one - electron states with energies of the order or less than thouless energy .",
    "the matrix elements of this hamiltonian are not just the matrix elements of the interaction potential ( [ eq:2.15 ] ) .",
    "this potential is defined in a much wider energy strip which includes one - electron states with energies @xmath199 .",
    "virtual transitions between the low - energy ( @xmath200 ) sector and these high - energy states renormalize the matrix elements of the universal hamiltonian .",
    "it turns out  @xcite that the third term in the hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.152 ] ) corresponding to the cooper channel of interaction , can be strongly renormalized by such virtual transitions . in order to avoid this complication",
    ", we will consider the case of the unitary ensemble in the discussion below , where the `` bare '' matrix elements corresponding to the cooper channel are already suppressed by a weak magnetic field ( it is sufficient to thread a flux of the order of unit quantum @xmath201 through the cross - section of a dot ) , and relegate the corresponding discussion of the interaction in the cooper channel to the appendix  [ ap:1 ] .",
    "omission of the cooper channel here is a simplification that will not affect our principal conclusions , as we will consider the case of repulsive interaction where the cooper channel , if it were included , is renormalized to zero anyway .",

    "so far , we have shown that the matrix elements of the hamiltonian of weak , short - range interaction are small compared to @xmath20 .",
    "therefore any observable quantity involving electron states within the energy strip @xmath244 around the fermi level , can be calculated by the lowest - order in @xmath253 perturbation theory .",
    "the situation is different for the long - range coulomb interaction @xmath254 where @xmath255 is the dielectric constant of the medium containing the electrons of the dot .",
    "does not account for the screening provided by the electrons of the dot .",
    "this screening will be considered in detail below . ]    for the simplest geometry , the corresponding matrix elements @xmath256 are inversely proportional to the _ linear _ size of the dot , rather than to its volume ( or area in dimension @xmath224 ) .",
    "if the linear size of the dot exceeds the screening radius ( or the effective bohr radius @xmath257 in @xmath224 ) , the matrix elements @xmath256 exceed @xmath20 , and the lowest - order perturbation theory in the interaction hamiltonian fails .    in the theory of linear screening , it is well - known how to deal with this difficulty .",
    "when calculating an observable quantity , one should take into account the virtual transitions of low - energy electrons into the high - energy states .",
    "if the gas parameter @xmath258 ( with @xmath259 being the electron fermi velocity ) of the electron system in the dot is small , then the random phase approximation ( rpa ) allows one to adequately account for such virtual transitions . accounting for these transitions yields , in general , a retarded electron - electron interaction  @xcite .",

    "finally we should mention that for a two - dimensional dot the relation @xmath196 holds only if the distance between the dot and gate exceeds the screening radius in the dot .",
    "so far we considered an isolated dot .",
    "we have established the validity of the universal rmt description both for the one electron hamiltonian and for the interaction effects .",
    "our goal now is to present a similar description for the connection of the dot with the external leads .",
    "we will assume that the leads contacting the dot are sufficiently clean , and neglect the mesoscopic fluctuations of the local density of states in the leads .",
    "in other words , we neglect closed electron trajectories in the leads that start at the contacts .",
    "we also neglect the electron - electron interaction in the leads . in the case of two - dimensional leads",
    ", this approximation is justified if the dimensionless conductance of the leads greatly exceeds the number of channels in the point contacts connecting leads to the quantum dot , or , equivalently , when the resistance of the leads is much smaller than the conductance of the point contacts .",
    "we wish to keep the rmt description of the dot . on the other hand",
    ", we saw that it is justified only for energy scales much smaller than thouless energy @xmath379 , where @xmath79 is the dimensionless conductance of the dot .",
    "the presence of point contacts with a total number of propagating modes @xmath11 broadens each level by an amount of the order of @xmath380 .",
    "hence , the use of the rmt description requires the condition @xmath381 where the dimensionless conductance of the dot is defined by eq .",
    "( [ g ] ) . since @xmath382 , the condition ( [ eq:2.55 ] )",
    "is met even if more than one channel is open .",
    "the conductance of a point contact connecting two clean conducting continua can be related , by the landauer formula  @xcite , to a scattering problem for electron waves incident on the contact .",
    "these waves can be labeled by a continuous wave number @xmath383 and by a set of discrete quantum numbers @xmath384 .",
    "the number @xmath383 accounts for the continuous energy spectrum of the incoming waves , and @xmath384 defines their spatial structure in the directions transverse to the direction of incidence .",
    "although in principle the number of discrete modes @xmath384 participating in scattering is infinite , the number of relevant modes contributing to the conductance is confined to the @xmath11 modes that are propagating through the contact ; all other modes are evanescent and hardly contribute to the conductance .",
    "an adiabatic point contact  @xcite is an example adequately described by a model having @xmath11 modes in a lead .",
    "let us now turn to a quantitative description of the theory .",
    "the total hamiltonian of the system is given as a sum of three terms @xcite , @xmath385 where the hamiltonian of the closed dot , @xmath386 , will be taken in the universal limit , see eq .",

    "_ the calculation of the statistical properties of the two - terminal conductance , the tunneling density of states , and the ground state energy is now reduced to the analysis of the properties of the scattering matrix for a chaotic quantum dot , which is a doable , though not straightforward task .",

    "this concludes our brief review of the two - terminal conductance , the tunneling density of states , and the ground state energy for a quantum dot in the absence of electron - electron interactions .",
    "the interaction between electrons leads to the coulomb blockade , and simple formulas as eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.63 ] ) , ( [ eq:2.69 ] ) , and ( [ eq : omegadopen ] ) cease to be valid . with interactions ,",
    "the answer very substantially depends on the conductance of the dot - lead junctions",
    ". the consideration of this regime will be the subject of the two remaining sections .",
    "in this section , we discuss the regime of strong coulomb blockade in quantum dots . to allow for this regime , the conductances of the contacts of the dot to the leads",
    "@xmath500 must be small in units of @xmath501 . as it was already explained in the introduction , junctions to a quantum dot formed in a two - dimensional electron gas of a semiconductor heterostructure",
    "are well described by the adiabatic point contact model . normally , a small conductance is realized only in single - mode junctions .",
    "since there are two leads connected to the dot , labeled @xmath13 and @xmath60 , we have total number of ( orbital ) channels @xmath502 , and the transmission block of the s - matrix of the point contacts has the form @xmath503 the transmission amplitudes for the separate left and right point contacts @xmath504 are related to the corresponding conductances by landauer formula ( [ eq:2.63 ] ) @xmath505 where the extra factor of two comes from the spin degeneracy .",
    "we recall that the coupling coefficients @xmath504 characterize only the point contact and are not random , see discussion after eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.58 ] ) ; they characterize the average conductance of each point contact and not the total conductance of a given sample consisting of both the two contacts and the quantum dot .    since the conductances @xmath506 and @xmath507 are small",
    ", we can express the coupling matrix @xmath394 relating the hamiltonian of the closed quantum dot to its scattering matrix in terms of @xmath506 and @xmath507 , see eq .",
    "( [ eq : rc ] ) , @xmath508 because the coupling is weak , it is possible to construct a perturbation theory of the conductance in terms of this coupling .",
    "this perturbation theory differs substantially for the peaks and the valleys of the coulomb blockade .",
    "these two cases will be considered separately .      in the weak tunneling regime ,",
    "the charge on the dot is well defined  quantum fluctuations of the charge are small  , and the particle number @xmath185 is quantized . in the course of an electron tunneling on and off the dot ,",
    "its charge varies by one .",
    "the activation energy for the electron transport equals the difference between the ground state energies of the hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.54a ] ) with two subsequent values of @xmath509 .",
    "a peak in the conductance as a function of @xmath510 occurs at those values of @xmath510 where the two ground states are degenerate .",
    "if one neglects the level spacing @xmath20 , the conductance peaks are equally spaced : @xmath511 . according to eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54a ] ) , the presence of a finite ( and fluctuating ) level spacing yields a random contribution to the spacings of the peaks .",
    "we will not discuss the mesoscopic fluctuations of the peak spacings , where a significant disagreement between the theory and experiments still exists ( see section v.e of the review  @xcite for a discussion ) , and concentrate on the amplitudes of the conductance peaks .    to describe the conductance peaks at low temperatures , @xmath512 ,",
    "it is sufficient to account only for the two charge states mentioned above , in which the dot carries @xmath509 and @xmath513 electrons , respectively , and does not have any particle - hole excitations . even under these simplifying circumstances",
    "the transport problem is not entirely trivial .",
    "every time the equilibrium number of electrons on the dot , @xmath509 , is odd , its state is spin - degenerate , which may result in the kondo effect .",
    "the transition between the spin - degenerate state and the singlet state occurs just at the gate voltages @xmath510 that correspond to the points of charge degeneracy @xmath514 . at these points ,",
    "the quantum dot attached to the leads is in a state similar to the mixed valence regime of an atom embedded in a metallic host material .",
    "we postpone the discussion of these delicate many - body phenomena till section  [ sec : kondo ] , and confine ourselves here to the results of the theory of rate equations .",
    "the applicability of this theory sets a lower limit for the temperature in the discussion below : @xmath7 must exceed the width @xmath515 of a discrete level broadened by the electron escape from the dot . at such temperatures ,",
    "the quantum coherence between the electron states on the dot and within the leads is not important . in this section",
    "we will also restrict ourselves to the case that only a single discrete level in the dot contributes to the current , _",
    "i.e. _ , we restrict ourselves to the temperature interval @xmath516 the case @xmath517 is briefly discussed in subsection [ sec : tdependence ] .",
    "the upper bound in eq .",
    "( [ eq:3.1.1 ] ) ensures that only the last occupied discrete level in the dot contributes to the electron transport . in the absence of the interaction",
    "this level can be in four states : we denote by @xmath518 the probability of this level to be occupied with one electron of given spin projection @xmath519 , by @xmath520 to be empty , and by @xmath521 to be occupied with two electrons .",
    "those probabilities are normalized as @xmath522 . if the level is adjusted in resonance with the fermi level in the leads , then due to the electron transfer through the dot , the state of the level changes between all of those states .",
    "the picture is changed when the interaction between electrons is included . as can be seen from eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54 ] ) , only three states with the number of electrons on the dot differing by 1 , can be in resonance .",
    "states with a different charge always have an activation energy of the order of the charging energy @xmath232 .",
    "as long as @xmath523 , these states do not participate in the electronic transport through the dot .",

    "we study the mesoscopic fluctuations of the conductance in the regime where the gate voltage @xmath510 is tuned away from the degeneracy point @xcite , @xmath579 . equations ( [ eq:3.1.4 ] ) and ( [ eq:3.1.5 ] ) predict in this case the conductance to be exponentially small @xmath580 $ ] . however , this expectation is not correct .",
    "the rate equations of sec .",
    "[ sec:3.1 ] take into account only processes which are of the first order in the right or left conductance . in these processes a charge is transferred from a lead ( initial state ) to the dot ( final state ) , or vise versa . in the valleys",
    "such processes are exponentially suppressed because of the high energy in the final state . on the other hand ,",
    "higher order processes allow for both the initial and final states to be in the leads , so that the thermal exponent does not appear .",
    "such processes , commonly referred to as co - tunneling  @xcite , are suppressed only algebraically , @xmath581 $ ] , and dominate the transport already at moderate deviations from the conductance peaks .",
    "such second - order processes are shown in fig .",
    "the processes ( a),(b ) and ( c),(d ) are electron - like and hole - like processes , respectively . in an electron - like process",
    ", the intermediate state corresponds to an extra electron placed on the dot . in this case",
    "the electrostatic part of the energy of the virtual state is given by [ see eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54a ] ) ] , @xmath582 where @xmath525 is the half - integer corresponding to the coulomb blockade peak . for a hole - like process",

    "the result is that in the cases ( b ) and ( d ) , the final state differs from the initial state by the excitation of an extra electron - hole pair ( inelastic co - tunneling ) .",

    "we recall that a relatively large correlation magnetic field in a valley results from a wide energy band ( @xmath649 ) of virtual discrete states in the dot . by the same token ,",
    "the conductance in adjacent valleys is also correlated , because all but one virtual states participating in transport are the same for such valleys .",
    "in fact the conductance remains correlated over a large number @xmath650 of valleys .",
    "the corresponding corellation function was calculated in ref .",
    "@xcite , and the valley - valley correlation function for the differential capacitances was found in ref .",
    "@xcite .    considering electron transport through a blockaded dot ,",
    "we have used so far finite - order perturbation theory in the dot - lead tunneling amplitudes .",
    "if the dot carries a non - zero spin , like in the case of an odd number of electrons on the dot , such a treatment may miss specific effects caused by the degeneracy of the spin state of an isolated dot .",
    "tunneling results in the exchange interaction between the spins of the dot and leads .",
    "the exchange , in turn , leads to a many - body phenomenon , the kondo effect .",
    "this effect results in an unexpected temperature dependence of the conductance across the dot at temperatures @xmath651 .",
    "the kondo effect is one of the most studied and best understood problems of many - body physics .",
    "initially , the theory was developed to explain the increase of resistivity of a bulk metal with magnetic impurities at low temperatures  @xcite .",
    "soon it was realized that kondo s mechanism works not only for electron scattering , but also for tunneling through barriers with magnetic impurities  @xcite .",
    "a non - perturbative theory of the kondo effect has predicted that the cross - section of scattering off a magnetic impurity in the bulk reaches the unitary limit at zero temperature  @xcite .",
    "similarly , the tunneling cross - section should approach the unitary limit at low temperature and bias  @xcite in the kondo regime .",
    "the kondo problem can be discussed in the framework of anderson s impurity model  @xcite .",
    "the three parameters defining this model are : the on - site electron repulsion energy @xmath404 , the one - electron on - site energy @xmath652 , and the level width @xmath653 formed by hybridization of the discrete level with the states in the bulk .",
    "the non - trivial behavior of the conductance occurs if the level is singly occupied , @xmath654 , and the temperature @xmath7 is below the kondo temperature @xmath655 where @xmath656 is measured from the fermi level  @xcite .    before considering the kondo effect in a quantum dot ,",
    "we first review it for tunneling through a single localized level with on - site repulsion @xmath404 using the hamiltonian of the anderson model , @xmath657 here @xmath658 , @xmath659 , and @xmath660 are the electron creation operators in the left and right leads ( @xmath13 and @xmath60 ) , and on the localized level , respectively ; @xmath661 are the corresponding energies in the electron continuum . for brevity ,",
    "the tunneling matrix elements @xmath662 and @xmath663 connecting the localized state in the dot with the states in the leads are taken to be @xmath664-independent .",

    "the number of electrons in the dot is controlled by the applied gate voltage . if this number is an odd integer , @xmath687 , _",
    "i.e. _ , the dimensionless gate voltage @xmath688 lies in the interval @xmath689 the kondo effect leads to a dramatic increase of the conductance at low temperatures .",
    "the consequence is an even - odd alternation of the valley conductance through the quantum dot : in `` even '' valleys , the low temperature conductance is due to elastic co - tunneling , while in `` odd '' valleys , the presence of an unpaired spin in the highest occupied level leads to the kondo effect , which causes a remarkable increase of the low temperature conductance compared to the even valleys .",
    "the advantage of using the quantum dots for the experimental studies of the kondo effect stems from an opportunity to effectively control the parameters of the system , which is hardly possible for a magnetic impurity embedded in a host material .",
    "quantitatively , the low - temperature limit for the conductance in the odd valleys is given by eqs .",

    "this is a very straightforward consequence of the coulomb blockade : out of the two elementary processes of charge transfer ( one is increasing , and another is decreasing the initial charge of the dot by @xmath24 ) , only one process is allowed .",
    "the important difference between the case of sequential tunneling through the quantum dot mentioned above and the process of elastic co - tunneling considered in section  [ sec:3.2 ] , is that for sequential tunneling each level contributes to a real process , rather than serves as a virtual state for tunneling as is the case for elastic cotunneling .",
    "therefore , for sequential tunneling not amplitudes , but the probabilities of tunneling through each level are added .    in the case of rapid inelastic relaxation , @xmath732 ,",

    "dispensing with the discreteness of the quasiparticle spectrum ( @xmath589 ) , one can estimate the lifetime of a state with a given charge as the @xmath758-constant of a circuit consisting of a capacitor with capacitance @xmath759 , imitating the dot , and a resistor with resistance @xmath760 , imitating the dot - lead contact . according to the heisenberg uncertainty principle ,",

    "we concentrate on the case of a narrow channel .",
    "] supporting a few propagating modes and connected adiabatically  @xcite to the lead and quantum dot at its ends .",

    "@xcite ] in this review , our aim is twofold . on the one hand , we want to present the detailed derivations that transform the problem into a one that can be solved using well - developed formalisms .",
    "on the other hand , we also want to give the general picture of the thermodynamic and transport properties of a weakly blockaded dot , as it emerges from the theory .",
    "therefore this section is organized as follows .",
    "we start with subsection  [ sec : overall ] , where an overview of the final results is given . for",
    "those readers who wish to enter into the more detailed derivations , this subsection may also serve as a guide to the more detailed presentations , which can be found in sections  [ sec : rigorous][sec : dos ] and appendices [ ap:3][ap:4 ] , and use a combination of the bosonization and perturbation theory methods . before presenting a rigorous treatment of the mesoscopic fluctuations ,",
    "we describe a simplified version of the theory in sections  [ sec : finitesize][sec : qualit ] .",
    "this version is still sufficient for performing the estimates of the most important observables .",
    "going beyond the estimates , however , requires a rigorous theory .",
    "it is necessary not only for fixing the numerical values of the coefficients in formulas for various measurable characteristics , but also for finding their dependence on control parameters .",
    "one can view the result for the correlation function of mesoscopic conductance fluctuations ( [ eq : mesoosc ] ) as an example .",
    "formalism and theory presented in sections  [ sec : rigorous][sec : dos ] were needed to predict the four - fold reduction of this function in the magnetic field  @xcite ; this prediction was later checked experimentally  @xcite .      _",

    "_ differential capacitance of an open dot . _",
    "+ in addition to complications stemming from quantum fluctuations of charge , the transport phenomena discussed here involve one more important part of many - body physics : the anderson orthogonality catastrophe  @xcite .",
    "this element becomes especially important in the analysis of conductance in a strongly asymmetric setup , see the discussion following eqs .",
    "( [ eq:40.13 ] ) and ( [ eq:80.4 ] ) .",
    "thermodynamic quantities are free from that complication",
    ". therefore measurement of a differential capacitance provides information additional to that found from the transport measurements .",
    "experimental investigation of the capacitance of a quantum dot is quite a challenging task  @xcite , and by now there were no systematic study of mesoscopic fluctuations of this quantity .    in presenting the theoretical results , we concentrate on the case of a dot connected to a single lead .",
    "we also assume that the junction allows for propagation of a single mode of electrons carrying both directions of spin ( small or no zeeman splitting ) .",

    "@xcite , @xmath818 the derivation of that result and its generalization to the case of many modes ( see also ref .",
    "@xcite ) is given in section  [ sec : cap ] , see eq .",

    "we have seen in this subsection , that there is a hierarchy of the energy scales characterizing an open dot .",
    "the charge of the dot fluctuates only at energy scales exceeding @xmath232 ; at lower energies these fluctuations are suppressed . however",
    ", strong fluctuations of the spin of the dot continues down to lower energies , @xmath798 see eq .",
    "( [ t0ex ] ) .",
    "if @xmath798 exceeds the level spacing @xmath20 , then at energies @xmath932 the spin of the dot is quantized , and may change only in quanta of @xmath933 due to the exchange interaction with the electrons in the lead ; at the same time , presence of many intra - dot excitations ( electron - hole pairs ) is allowed .",
    "finally , at energies below @xmath20 the intra - dot excitations are also suppressed . under these conditions ,",
    "the spin of the dot is @xmath370 or @xmath371 , depending on the sign of @xmath934 .",
    "if this cosine is positive , then the dot is in a singlet state , and there are no peculiarities in the temperature dependence of observable quantities at @xmath935 .",
    "however , if @xmath936 , then the dot carries a spin , and the kondo effect develops at sufficiently low temperatures . in the next subsection",
    "we will study the temperature domain @xmath935 , find the kondo temperature , and discuss the transport properties of the dot in kondo regime .",

    "in fact , the form of the hamiltonian ( [ exchange ] ) could be derived without resorting to the explicit calculation performed above within the bosonization technique .",
    "the only important notion needed for the derivation , is the low - energy decoupling of the dot from the lead .",
    "pinning of both charge and spin modes is the manifestation of this decoupling .",
    "the decoupling is complete , however , only in the absence of excitations . to describe the behavior of the system at low but finite temperatures",
    ", one needs to establish the least irrelevant operators that violate the complete decoupling .",
    "the decoupled dot and lead are described by independent fermi liquids .",
    "the number of electrons in the dot can not be changed , as such a variation of charge would result in a large energy increase of order @xmath232 .",
    "that is why the leading irrelevant operators preserving the initial @xmath191 symmetry are the interaction in the charge and spin channels between the dot and the lead at the point of contact , @xmath951 where @xmath952 is defined in eq .",
    "( [ exchange ] ) and @xmath953 and @xmath954 are the operators of the charge density in the dot ( @xmath955 ) and in the lead ( @xmath956 ) respectively , at the point @xmath945 of their contact .",
    "the first term here represents the interaction in the singlet channel ( inelastic scattering between an electron in the dot an electron in the lead ) . because the charge fluctuations are suppressed at energy @xmath232 which exceeds significantly the pinning energy of the spin mode @xmath957 , one finds @xmath958 .",
    "therefore , we can neglect the interaction in the singlet channel .",
    "moreover , even if this mode is taken into account , it does not lead to any non - trivial effect at low energies .",
    "the hamiltonians ( [ hpm ] ) , ( [ hz ] ) and ( [ exchange ] ) describe , in the bosonic and fermionic representation respectively , the low - energy properties of the very same system . correlation functions of observable quantities , calculated with the help of eqs .",

    "this fact will enable us to find the exact value of the coupling constant in the hamiltonian ( [ exchange ] ) .",
    "the advantage of the fermionic representation is that it allows for the description of the system at @xmath960 ( ultimately leading to the kondo effect ) .",

    "the detailed structure of the one - electron functions in the continuum of states @xmath965 is not important in the discussion of the kondo effect .",
    "an examination of the standard calculation  @xcite shows that only the densities @xmath966 , averaged over the continuum of states @xmath383 , matter .",
    "therefore we will suppress the indices @xmath967 and @xmath968 in the exchange constants hereinafter , assuming that the functions @xmath969 are normalized so that @xmath970    if the dot is in the spin - doublet state , the exchange constant gets renormalized at low energies . unlike the `` ordinary '' kondo model with only one localized orbital state involved , here the renormalization occurs due to virtual transitions in both the continuum spectrum of the lead and the discrete spectrum of the dot . to see the signature of the kondo effect",
    ", we calculate the second order correction to the exchange constant @xmath971 where @xmath12 labels the singly occupied level of the quantum dot .",
    "this second order correction , diagrammatically shown in fig .",
    "[ fig:530 ] , has the form @xmath972 where the integral is taken over the continuum energy spectrum @xmath973 in the leads , @xmath591 is the corresponding density of electron states .",
    "the sum over the discrete energy levels of electrons in the dot includes the term involving the singly occupied level @xmath974 .",
    "this term , which corresponds to a spin - flip within the same orbital level , @xmath975 , is responsible for the logarithmic singularity in the `` ordinary '' kondo effect .",
    "the rest of the terms in the sum correspond to the virtual transitions onto ( from ) the partially occupied level from ( to ) doubly - occupied ( empty ) electron levels .    at energies",
    "@xmath976 the discreteness of the spectrum is not important . if one neglects this discreteness all together the correction to the exchange constant is ultraviolet divergent @xmath977 .",
    "@xmath978 here @xmath979 is the one particle density of states in the dot .",
    "this divergent correction is similar to the irreducible vertex function in fermi liquid theory and can be incorporated into a new constant @xmath939 which can be numerically different from the bare constant .",
    "it is this `` new '' constant @xmath939 through which all observables at low energies are expressed .",
    "this condition allows us to exclude a large portion of the quasi - continuous spectrum of states in the dot at energies @xmath980 , and to relate the `` new '' constant @xmath981 in the fermion hamiltonian , which is valid at energies @xmath982 , to the constant in the boson hamiltonian ( [ hpm ] ) , ( [ hz ] ) , which does not have free parameters . to establish such a relation , one needs to consider a quantity that does not exhibit strong mesoscopic fluctuations , and therefore can be expressed in terms , insensitive to the particular values of the wave functions @xmath983 .",
    "the observable quantity to look at , is the spin magnetization of the dot caused by a magnetic field @xmath984 applied only to the lead .",
    "application of such a field results in a spin polarization , due to the pauli susceptibility , of electrons in the lead .",
    "this polarization , via the contact interaction , induces a finite spin polarization of the dot .",
    "such a calculation can be performed both in the bosonic and fermionic variables . in the boson variables ,",
    "the hamiltonian causing the perturbation of electrons in the lead has the form @xmath985 .",
    "this form , together with the hamiltonian of the free spin mode , eq .",
    "( [ hs0 ] ) , allows us to find the induced non - zero value of @xmath986 .",
    "this polarization , in turn , creates a perturbation @xmath987\\nabla\\theta_s(+0)$ ] for the spin mode in the dot , as seen from the hamiltonian ( [ hz ] ) .",
    "finally , the spin polarization of the dot @xmath988 can be evaluated by considering the just mentioned perturbation together with the unperturbed hamiltonian ( [ hs0 ] ) .",
    "the final result is @xmath310-independent and thus preserves its meaning in the limit @xmath989 . in a fermion representation",

    "note that the kondo conductance ( [ gklimit ] ) in a strongly asymmetric set - up is proportional to the product of the small conductance @xmath26 and small reflection coefficient @xmath1029 and therefore is significantly smaller than the conductance quantum @xmath501 even at @xmath701 .",
    "similar to the case of the closed quantum dot , the dominant mechanisms switch from inelastic co - tunneling at high temperatures to the elastic temperature - independent mechanism at lower temperatures , and finally to the regime of the kondo effect at the lowest temperatures .",
    "we postpone a more detailed discussion of those crossovers until after we have constructed a theory of elastic co - tunneling in open quantum dots .",
    "we turn to the outline of this theory in the following subsections .",
    "[ sec : qualit ]    as was already mentioned in the beginning of this section , the main difficulty for building a theory of interacting electrons in an open dot stems from the need to treat both the coulomb interaction and the dot - lead conductance non - perturbatively . in the limit @xmath589",
    ", the bosonization procedure allows one to treat exactly the interaction in a dot connected to a lead by a perfect quantum channel .",
    "then , the effect of a finite reflection amplitude @xmath796 in the channel can be treated by a systematic perturbation theory @xcite .",
    "an important conceptual conclusion drawn from this theory is that in the low - energy sector ( defined by @xmath1030 ) , the excitations inside and outside the dot are independent from each other .",
    "this understanding allowed us to consider the low - temperature effects ( @xmath935 ) in a partially open dot with @xmath1031 , because in this case one is able to map the properties of a partially - open dot onto the `` conventional '' case of strong coulomb blockade ( see the previous subsection ) .",
    "such a mapping allows one to consider the kondo effect , but is insufficient for evaluating the co - tunneling contribution to the conductance , for which a broad range of energies up to @xmath232 is involved .",
    "( this was shown , e.g. , in sec.[sec:3.2 ] , where we considered the valley conductance through a strongly blockaded quantum dot . )",
    "the aim of this and the following sections is to build a theory capable of describing simultaneously many - body effects and mesoscopic fluctuations at the intermediate range of energies , @xmath1032 .",
    "this section deals with a qualitative picture of the role of the mesoscopic fluctuations ; a rigorous calculation to verify the qualitative picture below is given in the following sections .",
    "let us first consider a completely opened channel ( @xmath865 ) . in the limit @xmath589 , the electron charge of the dot varies with the gate voltage as @xmath1033 , to ensure the minimum of the electrostatic energy @xcite .",
    "the interaction term in eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54a ] ) depends only on the number of electrons crossing the dot - channel boundary .",
    "since this information is represented as well in the asymptotic behavior of the wave - functions far from the entrance to the dot , such as the scattering phase shift , the properties of the ground state can be characterized by an analysis of those asymptotes . for the sake of simplicity",
    ", we consider the case of a dot connected to a lead by one channel , and consider spinless fermions instead of real electrons with spin .",
    "the ground state properties at low energy can then be understood from the following argument .",
    "the entrance of an additional electron with energy @xmath204 ( all the energies will be measured from the fermi level ) into the dot requires the charging energy @xmath232 .",
    "therefore , the electron may spend a time of the order of @xmath1034 in the dot , after which the extra charge accumulated on the dot has to relax .",
    "one can distinguish two processes that lead to charge relaxation : ( i ) elastic process where the same electron leaves the dot , and ( ii ) inelastic process where another electron is emitted from the dot . at low energies",
    "the probability of the inelastic process is small as @xmath1035 , by virtue of the smallness of the phase volume .",
    "( the last statement assumes fermi liquid behavior at low energies and , as we will see later , is valid only for the spinless one - channel case . ) therefore , for @xmath1036 , we may conclude that an incoming electron spends a time of the order @xmath1037 inside the dot , after which it bounces back into the channel without creating excitations .",
    "the same consideration is applicable to an electron attempting to leave the dot .",
    "the fact that within the energy range @xmath1038 from the fermi level the electron processes are predominantly elastic implies that the low energy properties of the system can be mapped onto a dot effectively decoupled from the channel , that there is a well - defined scattering amplitude from the entrance of the dot , and that the phase of this scattering amplitude is given by the friedel sum rule @xmath1039 equation  ( [ phaseshift ] ) can be applied to electrons incident from inside the dot , as well as to electrons incident from the channel .",
    "the description outlined here resembles closely nozieres fermi liquid description of the unitary limit in the one - channel kondo problem @xcite .",
    "we now demonstrate that the above considerations are sufficient to reproduce the result @xmath1040 obtained by matveev  @xcite for the ground state energy @xmath1041 of spinless fermions in the limit of zero level spacing @xmath20 in the dot and with a finite reflection amplitude @xmath796 in the contact , and then apply the same scheme to find the corrections to the ground state energy arising from a finite @xmath20 , but without @xmath796 .",
    "those corrections will result in the mesoscopic fluctuations of the ground state energy .",

    "we now proceed with an exposition of the general formalism used to calculate the capacitance , tunneling density of states , and conductance of an interacting quantum dot , without neglecting the effect of mesoscopic fluctuations of the wavefunction in the dot .",
    "( that is , without neglecting the possibility that an electron that has entered the dot will return coherently to the point contact . )",
    "the first step is to reformulate the problem in terms of an effective action that accounts for these coherent returns .",
    "our formal starting point is the same as in sec .",
    "[ sec:2.2 ] : the hamiltonian of the dot connected to the leads is written as the sum of a hamiltonian of the closed dot , a hamiltonian of the leads , and a term @xmath388 coupling the lead and the dot , @xmath1078 here , the hamiltonian of the dot is , in turn , written as a sum of the hamiltonian @xmath1079 of the closed dot in the absence of electron - electron interactions and the charging energy @xmath1080 [ see also eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54a ] ) ; here spin is included in the indices @xmath250 and @xmath252 ] @xmath1082 the hamiltonian @xmath387 of the leads is given by eq .",

    "equations ( [ eq:30.482 ] ) and ( [ eq : action ] ) provide an effective description of the combined system of the lead and the dots in terms of fermions moving in one - dimensional wires , where the interaction only exists on one end of the wire . the effective action @xmath1128 provides a coupling between the wires and between left and right moving fermions .",

    "the approximation ( [ eq:30.490 ] ) loses all the information about the trajectories where the electron returns to the entrance of the dot , after having been reflected by the dot s walls or by impurities inside the dot .",
    "such returns are the cause of mesoscopic fluctuations of the capacitance and other observable quantities .",
    "mesoscopic fluctuations are present in the full action ( [ eq : action ] ) , which is non - local in time .",

    "there is a good physical reason to distinguish the two contributions to the tunneling density of states in eq .",
    "( [ eq:40.9 ] ) .",
    "the first contribution in ( [ eq:6.18b ] ) is inelastic : this term does not allow the introduced electron to leave the dot ; the charge of the dot at the moment of tunneling suddenly changes by @xmath1198 and all the other electrons have to redistribute to accommodate this charge .",
    "we will see , that the logarithmical divergence of the imaginary time action corresponding to such evolution ( orthogonality catastrophe ) completely suppresses this contribution at @xmath1214 .",
    "conversely , the second contribution , @xmath1215 , cf .",
    "( [ eq:6.18c ] ) , contains the kernel @xmath1216 which promotes the tunneled electron through the dot into the channel ( left lead ) .",
    "because the very same tunneling electron is introduced to and then removed from the dot , there is no need in the redistribution of other electrons , so no orthogonality catastrophe occurs . as a result ,",
    "the elastic contribution survives at @xmath1214 , analogously to the elastic co - tunneling contribution to the conductance of a strongly blockaded dot , see sec .",

    "= 0.4    imagine now that we expand an observable quantity in power series in @xmath1268 and account in each order of perturbation theory only for the pole contributions in the integrals over the intermediate times @xmath1269 .",
    "the pole contribution in each order does not depend on the interaction , and constitutes just a green function for non - interacting fermions .",
    "such contributions can be easily summed up , resulting in a geometric series in @xmath310 . ) of the entire system , including the contribution @xmath1097 from the closed dot . ] since a geometric series of the matrix @xmath310 is precisely the scattering matrix @xmath357 , cf.eq .",
    "( [ eq:30.49 ] ) , we thus arrive at the following simple result : in order to take into account the pole contributions in _ all _ subsequent orders of perturbation theory , one has to simply replace @xmath310 in the first non - vanishing contribution by @xmath1270 ( here @xmath1271 is the fermionic matsubara frequency . )    consider now a correlation function which includes a branch cut in the leading order ( _ e.g. _ , as function of the times @xmath1272 in second order in the effective action ) .",
    "then , in each of the subsequent higher orders we select the contributions including only one branch cut , all other singularities in these terms being single poles .",
    "since such a contribution is factorised into a branch cut factor involving two times , and a product of green functions for non - interacting fermions for the remaining times , we can again sum up all such contributions as a geometric series .",
    "as before , the result is that one has to take the first non - vanishing term in an expansion in powers of @xmath310 that contains a single branch cut and then make the replacement ( [ eq : lsall ] ) to account for all higher orders in @xmath310 with the same branch cut singularity .",
    "in such a way , we take into account all the orders of perturbation theory in @xmath1148 that contain only one branch cut singularity in each order .",
    "the same analytic structure occurs in all higher orders of perturbation theory : poles give a `` reducible '' average , whereas the `` irreducible '' part of the propagator has only branch cut singularities .",
    "this leads to a very important statement : _ the perturbation theory in the action ( [ eq:30.482 ] ) can be constructed as an expansion in powers of the scattering matrix @xmath357 rather than of the kernel @xmath310_. in this expansion all the reducible averages ( poles ) are included automatically in all the orders of the perturbation theory , whereas the branch cuts are considered perturbatively ; each order of of the perturbation theory in @xmath357 is characterized by the number of branch cuts it includes . ) and the conductance , eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.63 ] ) , are of second order in the scattering matrix @xmath357 . in the effective action theory ,",
    "this result follows from the summation of the pole contributions to all orders in @xmath310 , which produces a single term proportional to @xmath1273 .",
    "the interaction corrections , however , can be of higher order in @xmath357 , depending on the number of branch cut singularities that are included in the perturbation theory . ]",

    "( [ eq:50.10 ] ) , the renormalization of the scattering amplitude is complete , _",
    "i.e. _ , the same as for the direct reflection from the contact we studied before . on the other hand ,",
    "the effect of interaction on the scattering events occurring `` deep inside '' the dot , @xmath1379 is exponentially weak . as long as the temperature is sufficiently high , @xmath1380 , and the scattering from the dot is ergodic , the majority of the scattering events is not renormalized by the interaction .",
    "therefore , the landauer part of the conductance ( [ eq:70.7 ] ) remains intact at such temperatures .",
    "the interaction correction affects only a small portion of scattering events , and thus only slightly affects the statistics of the two terminal conductance .",

    "( [ eq:70.11 ] ) . at high temperature ,",
    "the interaction correction is less significant than the correction from the weak localization .",
    "notice , however , that at @xmath1394 , which is the lower limit of the applicability of the theory , the interaction correction is smaller than the weak localization correction only by parameter @xmath1395 , and may be still important for the temperature dependence of magnetoresistance .",
    "one notices also that for the unitary ensemble , @xmath71 , both the weak localization and interaction corrections to the average conductance vanish , in contrast with the usual situation in disordered metals @xcite .",
    "the reason is that the interaction enhances any electron scattering , see eq .",
    "( [ eq:70.11 ] ) , no matter whether it is scattering from one lead to the other ( @xmath1396 ) or backscattering into the same lead ( @xmath1397 and @xmath1398 ) .",
    "for the unitary ensemble , the scattering @xmath1397 and @xmath1399 occur with equal probabilities and therefore neither reflection nor transmission are enhanced in average . on the other hand for the orthogonal ensemble",
    ", backscattering into the same lead is more probable due to the weak localization , and the interaction further increases the backscattering probability .    in a similar manner ,",
    "the mesoscopic fluctuations are also affected by the electron - electron interaction .",

    "equation ( [ eq:80.4 ] ) is valid for reflectionless point contacts , provided that @xmath1423 .",
    "note that eq .",
    "( [ eq:80.4 ] ) predicts a power - law temperature dependence of the tunneling conductance .",
    "the power - law factor can be understood in terms of the well - known orthogonality catastrophe  @xcite .",
    "an addition of an electron without a re - distribution of charge between the dot and lead would cost an amount of energy @xmath1424 .",
    "it means that the tunneling spectrum would have a `` hard '' gap with the width of the order of charging energy , and the temperature dependence of the conductance would display an activation behavior .",
    "the power - law ( [ eq:80.4 ] ) indicates that a redistribution of charge indeed occurs when an additional electron tunnels onto the dot .",
    "in fact , each channel of the ideal dot - lead junction carries away charge @xmath1425 . according to the friedel sum rule",
    ", it corresponds to an additional phase shift @xmath1426 for the scattering in each of the channels .",
    "tunneling of an electron with energy @xmath1427 creates an excited state of the electron system consisting of the dot and lead .",
    "the overlap of this state with the initial state of the system defines the probability of tunneling .",
    "the smaller the energy @xmath204 , the smaller such overlap is ( orthogonality catastrophe  @xcite ) .",
    "this overlap can be expressed in terms of the phase shifts  @xcite , and is proportional to @xmath1428 , where @xmath1429 , and the sum is taken over all the modes . in our case , the charge is `` shifted '' through @xmath11 channels inside the dot , and through the same number of channels in the lead , yielding @xmath1430 equal contributions to the sum ; @xmath1431 .",
    "this exponent indeed coincides with the one in the power law ( [ eq:80.4 ] ) .    a particular case of eq .",
    "( [ eq:80.4 ] ) for one - channel junctions deserves additional discussion . for spinless fermions , @xmath1275 , one obtains",
