    "in the beginning of this review , see subsections  [ sec:2.1]-[sec : hfinal ] , we have derived the model hamiltonian of an isolated dot .",
    "one of the main assumptions in that derivation was that the electron states are random .",
    "randomness of the one - electron states , a large dimensionless conductance inside the dot ( @xmath1464 ) , and relative weakness of the electron - electron interaction ( @xmath1465 ) allowed for a relatively simple description of an isolated dot .",
    "the main part of the hamiltonian of the dot is universal ; it consists of a free - electron part described by random matrix theory and an interaction term , which is not random , see eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54 ] ) .",
    "corrections to this universal part of the hamiltonian are small at @xmath111 . in",
    "the discussion of the transport phenomena and of other effects which result from the contact of the dot with external electron reservoirs ( leads ) , we have considered that universal part of the hamiltonian only . despite this extremely simple description of the physics inside the quantum dot , a large variety of intricate physical effects is uncovered when the dot is coupled to the outside world via point contacts .",
    "these effects range from quantum interference transport phenomena in the regime strong coulomb blockade ( subsections  [ sec:3.1 ] and [ sec:3.2 ] ) to the effects of quantum charge fluctuations and non - fermi liquid behavior of partially open quantum dots ( subsection  [ sec : open ] ) .",
    "remarkably , the low temperature behavior of transport through a quantum dot with a finite spin is always dominated by the kondo effect , see subsections  [ sec : kondo ] and [ sec : exchange ] .    in this concluding section , we will mention three areas of research on quantum effects in quantum dots that are not covered in this review .",
    "the first area is related to the problem of electron relaxation in a constrained geometry .",
    "it is well - known that in a bulk clean fermi liquid the relaxation rate of an electron with energy @xmath204 is @xmath1466 . in a confined system , an electron occupying a discrete level with energy @xmath204 can decay with the excitation of an electron - hole pair .",
    "it was shown in ref .",
    "@xcite that the relaxation rate @xmath1467 still scales as @xmath1468 with the electron energy . ) in second order perturbation theory . ] the quadratic dependence of the inelastic relaxation rate on the the electron energy reflects the smallness of the phase volume of the final state , and , therefore , is the same for the quantum dots and for the clean fermi liquid .",
    "the proportionality coefficient is , however , much larger than its value for the clean system , which reflects the stronger correlation of one - particle states of the disordered dot in comparison with the plane waves .",
    "nevertheless , @xmath1469 for @xmath1470 , which justifies the one particle approximation as the starting point for isolated quantum dot .",
    "the treatment of ref .",
    "@xcite neglected the discreteness of the spectrum of the final states .",
    "the question of the validity of such an approach was first addressed in ref .",
    "@xcite where it was shown that the approximation of the one particle density of states by the discrete levels broadened to @xmath1471 is correct only at energies larger than @xmath1472 . at such energies , the three particle state obtained as a result of one - particle decay will decay further into five - particle state , etc .",
    ", thus resulting in a true decay , without the possibility of a return to the initial state .",
    "if the energies of the initial state is smaller than @xmath1473 , the three particle state is not strongly connected to the five particle state , so that the quantum dot will return to the original state . in that case , the level is broadened much less than it is found in ref .",
    "@xcite .",
    "inelastic processes within the dot affect the conductance through the dot .",
    "this is exemplified in the temperature dependence of the conductance of an open quantum dot , eq .",
    "( [ eq:70.12 ] ) .",
    "it follows from this formula , that the weak localization correction ( second term ) does not depend on temperature .",
    "this is , however , a consequence of neglecting the inelastic process within the dot . only due to the those processes ,",
    "the phase coherence inside the dot is destroyed .",
    "quantitatively , it is described approximately @xcite by the replacement @xmath1474 with @xmath1475 equal to the inelastic relaxation time for an electron with energy @xmath7 . from the theory ,",
    "one expects @xmath1476 .",
    "experiments with open quantum dots @xcite give the result @xmath1477 .",
    "the reasons for such discrepancy have not been identified as of yet .",
    "the second area of research omitted in this review is related to the spin - spin interactions .",
    "these effects become significant at @xmath1478 , and may result in a formation of a dot ground state with spin exceeding @xmath349 .",
    "sufficiently strong electron - electron interaction ( large @xmath337 ) should result in a complete spin polarization ( stoner instability ) .",
    "however , fluctuations of the density of orbital levels may result in an anomalously large spin of a finite - size sample even at moderate values of @xmath337 .",
    "this problem was studied in refs .",
    "the simplest manifestation of the anomalous spin polarization is the transition from a singlet to triplet state in a dot when the number of electrons is even .",
    "such a transition can be achieved by a decrease of the spacing between the doubly - occupied level and the next empty orbital state . in very small quantum dots",
    ", the level separation can be controlled experimentally by application of a magnetic field that affects the electron orbital motion  @xcite .",
    "the singlet - triplet transition can be seen experimentally in a measurement of the conductance through the dot  @xcite as it results in the increase of kondo temperature at the transition point  @xcite . in larger dots",
    ", it can also be seen by the parametric dependence of coulomb blockade peaks on the magnetic field , which shows a kink at the single - triplet transition @xcite , or a change in the peak - to - peak correlations from neighboring peaks to next - neighboring peaks @xcite .",
    "sofar , the effect of the anomalous spin polarization on the conductance was considered only in the regime of weak tunneling .",
    "the counterpart of this effect for the strong tunneling regime has not been studied .",
    "finally , we have not discussed the effects of a time - dependent change of the shape of the dot by external gates ; this effect is described by the first term in eq .",
    "( [ eq:2.54 ] ) .",
    "we mention here only the suppression of the weak localization correction in quantum dots and generation of a dc - current by a time depenedent perturbation @xcite .",

    "[ sec : interaction ] , the universal description of the interaction by hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.152 ] ) is valid provided that the coupling constants in this hamiltonian are calculated with taking into account virtual transitions to the excited states which are beyond the energy strip in which the hamiltonian ( [ eq:2.152 ] ) is defined . for a weak short range interaction , these transitions only insignificantly change the interaction constants @xmath232 and @xmath332 for the charge and spin channels , respectively .",
    "the situation is different for the cooper channel , where the renormalization is significant even for a weak interaction .",
    "consider the lowest order perturbation theory correction to the interaction matrix element @xmath1494 shown in fig .",
    "[ figap1]a .",
    "= 0.6    the analytic expression for this correction is @xmath1495 according to the structure of the matrix elements discussed in sec .",
    "[ shortrange ] , the largest contribution comes from the terms with @xmath1496 , and one finds @xmath1497 where @xmath1498 is a high energy cut - off above which the approximation of the instantaneous interaction and equidistant spectrum becomes non - applicable . because of the large logarithmic factor here , the renormalization of the coupling constants in the cooper channel is significant , even if the interaction is weak , @xmath1499 .    to take into account this renormalization",
    ", one has to sum the leading logarithmically divergent series shown in fig .",
    "[ figap1 ] b. this results in the renormalization of the interaction constant in comparison with its bare value , @xmath1500    one can see , that for repulsive interaction , @xmath1501 , the effective interaction in the cooper channel is always weak , and for the majority of effects it can be neglected form the very beginning . for the attractive interaction , @xmath195 , the interaction constant renormalizes to strong coupling limit and diverges at the energy scale @xmath1502 , which is nothing but the superconducting gap in bcs theory .",

  "abstract_text": [
    "<S> we review the quantum interference effects in a system of interacting electrons confined to a quantum dot . </S>",
    "<S> the review starts with a description of an isolated quantum dot . </S>",
    "<S> we discuss the random matrix theory ( rmt ) of the one - electron states in the dot , present the universal form of the interaction hamiltonian compatible with the rmt , and derive the leading corrections to the universal interaction hamiltonian . </S>",
    "<S> next , we discuss a theoretical description of a dot connected to leads via point contacts . </S>",
    "<S> having established the theoretical framework to describe such an open system , we discuss its transport and thermodynamic properties . </S>",
    "<S> we review the evolution of the transport properties with the increase of the contact conductances from small values to values @xmath0 . in the discussion of transport </S>",
    "<S> , the emphasis is put on mesoscopic fluctuations and the kondo effect in the conductance . </S>",
    "<S> + pacs numbers : 73.23.hk , 73.23.-b , 72.10.bg    coulomb blockade ; mesoscopic fluctuations ; random matrix theory ; bosonization ; kondo effect </S>"
  ]
